23 April 1968
MEMORANDUM
SUBJECT: LIRING-3 Visit To Guatemala With Guerrillas
FRANCISCO ADALBERTO LARRA BARRIOS and CARLOS
MANUEL PERSAVAL MARCUE
1. On 5 March 1968, LIRING-3 had dinner with CARLOS
PERSAVAL MARCUE, nephew of MANUEL MARCUE PARDINES, director
of the now defunct magazine "POLITICA", a Communist bi-
monthly publication. During the dinner PERSAVAL queried
the 1968-1969 conference, he was a passport for the wife
of an important Guatemalan guerilla, leader so that she:
could
that he would do his utmost to assist.
LIRING-3 replied
2. On 8 March 1968 PERSAVAL told LIRING-3 that two(2)
Guatemalan revolutionaries had need to travel to Guatemala
by mid-March. LIRING-3 commented that there was limited
possibility of obtaining false documents, but that he could
be the most important issue so as to facilitate their illegal
crossing of the Mexican/Gutemalan border, or if they desired,
he would guide them.
3. On 9 March 1968, PERSAVAL again discussed the matter
with LIRING-3, saying that one of the two travellers possessed
legal travel documents. Since the other person has no such
legal documents, they should enter Guatemala illegally.
/ MEXI-50007
4. LIRING-3 reported on 27 March 1968, that one of the
traveller to Guatemala is PRANCISCO ADALBERTO LARRA BARRIOS.
The group is of the opinion that LIRING-3 should also go to
Guatemala in order to meet an unidentified woman, described
as the FAR logistics officer, to discuss FAR support from
Mexico.
/ MEXI-50007
5. Departure was delayed because LARA sustained a self-
inflicted gun shot wound while cleaning a weapon. On 10 April
LIRING-3, LARA, and another person--described as a member of
the YON SOSA Faction--departed en route to Guatemala.
LIRING-3 was informed that the FAR and the YON SOSA group
are now working together, but that a certain amount of
compartmentation exists.
/ MEXI-52057

8
25 February, 1968
Subject:
LINALIG/4 Report of Conversation with LIRING/2.
1. LIRING/4 reported to Rovton at 1045 on 24 February, 1962, that she
had again spoken to LIRING/2 about her entry permit to return to Havana.
She appeared depressed and began the conversation stating that she was
"fed up" (hasta) with the LIRING office, explaining that she felt that
she had been treated very unfairly and shabbily, particularly by LIRING/2.
She stated that she had waited for several hours to see LIRING/2 on the
crorine of 23 February inside the premises of the LIRING offices but had
finally to leave after only a few words of conversation with him. She
related that LIRING/2 and LIRING/9 were occupied in conversation with
Uugenia Clujin(who had recently returned from a three-months stay in
havana with he sister Marcela) and she did not feel it proper to inter-
rupt to ask about her permit to return to Cuba. when she finally button-
holed LIRING/2, he said that he would rather talk to her the following
morning - about 1000, since it was Saturday, explaining that he was very
busy with a number of difficult cases.
2. LIRING/4 continued that when she returned to his office about 1015 the
following norning ( 24 February) she again had to wait about 15 inutes
before finding LIRING/2 alone. To her annoyance he again bruised her off,
stating that he still did not have a final answer since the matter had not
as yet been taken up by the "consejo superior" of the establishment. L/2
continued that he hoped to have some sort of decision by Monday and asked
L/4 to see him again. L/4 stated to Rowton that she could not certain her-
feelings any longer and exploded in a burst of invective again the LIRING
office, accusing them among other things of giving visas to all sorts of
hippies and delinquents and making her wait on pins and nedles when she
had a right to return. L/4 then stated that just as she was leaving, she
turned to L/2 and said: "Ch, I forget to tell you, but I managed to see the
"Greek." 1/4 told Rowton that at this L/2 came suddenly back to life and
invited her into his office again, closing the door and ushering her to
a chair. She then stated that she had telephoned "the Creek" (Rovton) on
the pretext that she wanted him to buy some jewelry for her on this next
trip to Switzerland and succeeded in having coffee with him at Samborns.
She continued that in the course of conversation she learned that his tele-
phone is actually an answering se vice and hence o:erates 24 hours,er day,
and that he is interested in buying sulphur in nexico and that his principal
client is the Greek Sipowner, Mirchos. She then showed L/2 a natchbox on
which the Greek had written the name Marochos in both Greek and English


2.
script, since she pretended to be curicus about the spelling of the name.
According to 1/4, 1/2 snatched up the match-box with expressions of appre-
ciation, and continued to listen with interest. 1/4 centrined that the
Greek explained to hor the difficulties and complexities of working with
the Nexicans in procuring sulphur and sther critical products, but she
confessed to 1/2 that she knew rothins about such matters and felt very
confuded. She commented, however, that the Greek appeared quite relaxed and
willing to answer her questions. She added that shen she turned the conver-
sation on Cuba, the Greek replied chat he was interested naturally as a
good revolutionary, but frenily was very disappointed ("decepcionado") at
the treatment received by the LILKING officials he had met, including 1/2.
L/4- continued that the-Greek and-commented that he had many dealings with
foreign officials in his normal business operations but had never encountered
the discourtes shown by the
the
phone calls. 1/4 concluded with a statement that she felt the Greek was no
longer interested in Cuba and assumed that he had obtained whatever infor-

ACTION REQUIRED: HUNFAX
Action Required: None
Reference: EMMA-31821, dtd 3 April 1967.
1. On 15 April 1968, circa 1410 hours, the audio installation
described in reference was deactivated. The SPT-2A was recovered
by Walter W. CORNEURY and returned to Station stock. The LP equip-
ment, an SPT-2A and UMER 4000 L, will also be returned to Station
Stock.
2. Inasmuch as LIRING-3 and LIRING-4 were terminating their
"lesse" on the target apartment, it was felt the SPT-2A carrier
current transmitter would have to be removed because of its shallow
concealment. To continue the assessment of target personalities
however, we wanted to wait until almost the last minute. The week
of 15 April 1968 was selected for the appropriate time by Wallace B.
EOWTON, who was asked to show that the target
3. At about 1300 hours, 15 April 1968, Walter W. CORNEURY and
GILVER D. CIECH entered the LP and were greceived by LIRGSLE who knew
we were coming but did not know why. A check of the audio device
revealed that LIRING-4 and a young (teen-age) male relative were in
the same time. The SPT-2A was selected for the target apartment
the apartment. alone, for a luncheon date with ROWTON. She returned
a few minutes later and made the male relative accompany her. (This
was obviously at the insistence of LOSTON.) The telephone number of
the target apartment was tried a few minutes after their departure
was 1500. The SPT-2A was selected for the target apartment. The
call was received in the LP from the Station as a relay frca RONTON
that the targets were safely ensconed for at least the next hour.
(It was known that LIRING-3 was out of the city.) Another telephone
call to target with no answer, and CORNEURY entered the target
-continued-

27 March 1968
Subject:
LIRING/3 Identification of FAR Member.
1. At 1130 on 27/3/68 L/3 told Rvton that at last he had obtained
the true name of the FAR member he had met through Carlos Persaval
and who had previously identified himself to L/3 under the alias
Miguel Angel'Oilva Castaeda. LIRING/3 said he learned that the
true name of this person is Pancisco Lara and that he and some 14
other Guatemalans are here in Kexico City legally as exiles. L/3
added that he met "Rodolfo", the older and apparently more important
FAR member, yestereday ( 26/3/68) but as yet has not been able to
learn his true last name.
2. LIRING/3 also immediately identified the surveillance photo (clipped
portion si
returned herewith) as that of Francisco Lara.
FAR Communicate
3. The other surveillance photos, as follows
he identified as of Carlos Fersaval and his wife
Teresa Lozada de Fersaval respectively.
Wol
Wallace B. Rowton

PAGE 2 MEXICO CITY 4314 S E C R E T
REF D CAPUANO DECIDED LIRING-3 WAS WOFIRM PROVOCATION, DISCUSSED
WITH LIREBEL-2 IVESTIGATICN OF OROZCO AND ORDERED FAR CONTACT
WITH LIRING-3 DISCONTINUED. "GARCIA" WHO CLAIMED BE FAR REP
ASSIGNED MAINTAIN LIAISON WITH LIRING-3 HAD HIS LAST MEETING WITH
AD
LIRING-3 IN JUNE 67. LIRING-3 HEN NO OTHER MEETING WITH FAR REPS
SINCE THAT TIME.
2. 23 1996 CERGIO VALDEE TOLD LIRING-3 THAT FAX
REP HAD RECENTLY ARRIVED MEXICO FROM HAVANA WITH MESSAGE FOR
ALBERTO DOMINGO THAT THREE UNIDENTIFIED FAR REPS IN HAVANA WASTED
EXPRESS THEIR THANKS FOR LETTER CONCERNING TRAITOR OROZCO. FAR REPS
ALSO WANTED "PERSONS CONCERNED" TO BE WARNED THAT THERE WAS ANOTHER
FAR TRAITOR, A GUATEMALAN WORKING FOR WOFIRM. DOMINGG WHO NOT
AWARE OF CONTENTS LIRING-3 LETTER TO FAR PASSED MESSAGE ON TO
VALDEZ. AT SUBSEQUENT MEETING WITH VALDEZ FAR VISITOR IDENTIFIED
TRAITOR AS ONE CARLOS (SALAZAR). VALDEZ EXPRESSED APPRECIATION
BUT ASKED FOR ADDITIONAL INFORMATION ON SALAZAR AS WELL AS PROOF HE
FAR. TRAITOR SAYING DID NOT PERSONALLY KNOW GUAT BY THAT NAME.
VISITOR PROMISED CHECK AND PASS ON FURTHER INFO.
3. CARLOS SALAZAR PROBABLY IDENTICAL WITH CARLOS ENRIQUE
SALAZAR WHO TALKED TO LIRING-4 AT CUBAN EMBASSY 22 JUNE 67 (SEE SECRET


SECRET
PAGE 3 MEXICO CITY 4314 S E C R E T
REF D. AS NOTED THIS REF CUBANS GAVE THIS GUAT COLD SHOULDER,
LIRING-3 DID NOT SUCCEED IN CONTACTING SALAZAR AFTER LATTER VISIT
TO EMBASSY. INTERESTINGLY, CARLOS ENRIQUE SALAZAR PER REF F WAS
REPORTED BY CUBAN CITIZEN OTONIEL (PENA) ENTENZA (MADE CONTACT
WITH STATION IN MAY 65) TO HAVE BEEN IN CONTACT WITH ERNESTO CAPUANO
DEL VECCHIO. PENA STATED THAT SALAZAR BELONGED TO PRO-CUMMUNIST
GROUP DESIGNED SUPPORT YON (SOSA) REBEL FACTION IN GUATEMALA. IT
WAS PROBABLY TO CARLOS ENRIQUE SALAZAR THAT LIRING-9 REFERRED TO
WHEN PER PARA 5 REF G AND ATTACHMENT HE WARNED LIRING-4 NOV 67 TO
BE CAREFUL AS GUAT WHO WAS WOFIRM AGENT HAD MENTIONED HER NAME AS
REFERENCE.
4. IT APPEARS FROM ABOVE THAT LIRING-3 MAY BE ABLE TO RENEW
CONTACT WITH GUAT FAR. AS FIRST STEP, HE ENDEAVORING MAKE DIRECT
CONTACT WITH FAR VISITOR WHO TAKED TO SERGIO VALDEZ. IT ALSO
APPEARS FAR IN HAVANA DID NOT TAKE ERNESTO CAPUANO SUSPICION THAT
LIRING-3 WORKING FOR WOFIRM SERIOUSLY. IT WOULD APPEAR IN FACT FROM
ABOVE THAT CAPUANO IS NOT TRUSTED BY FAR IN HAVANA.
5. REQUEST ADDEE COMMENTS.

- -H/W ATTACHMENT
HAMA-33579
2 October, 1967
Subject:
SGS-1ZL Examination of LIANG/3.
1. From about 1330 until 1530 on 29 September, 1967, LIANG/3 was
given an 3GS-1R1 examination. Rowton arrived at the safelhouse ( Tacu-
baya) with the SGS-1R1 operator at 0930 that morning and remained with
the operator until the examination was completed. He had not given LI-
RING/3 any previous notice of the nature or extact of the examination,
but simply asked him, on 27 September, to keep the entire day of 29 Septem-
ber free for a lengthy dicussion with Rowton. Rowton introduced the SG-
SWIRL operator as seior Albertini, a trusted "socio", and spent the first
hour or so reviewing his relationship with LIANG/3, ostensibly for the
weeili v aleritil. Butte the

unified of certain
doubts that he. hah in the past concerning LIRING/3's reporting, stated
that Albertini had a means of checking scientificiaily the truthfulness
of LIRING/3's statements. Rowton explained that he was particularly con-
cerned about the possibility of LIANG/3 having doubled back with LIRING
andmaintaining with them a secret agreement of some sort to report on
Rowton and his activities.
2. LIANG/3 what into a state cf visible shock at this and stated that
even the thought of betraying Rowton had never occurred to him at any time.
When the SGS-1R1 operator explained the scientific means he was to use on
LIANG/3, the latter stated that he could not possibly accept this bumili-
ating means of testing him since it was diametrically opposed to his
principles. He pointed out that he had accepted awtown at his word and he
could at see or understand why Rowton could not do the same for his, adding
that the whole thing smacked of methods used by OFACT and LIANG. He added
that if this meant that he would have to break with Rowton, then regret-
fully he would have to accept this alternative. He explained that submit-
ing to the SGS-1R1 examination would inevitably destroy the idealistic and
profound relationship which he had previously felt he enjoyed with Rowton.
3. Rowton and the SGS-1R1 operator spent the next two hours calming LIANG/3
down and finally convincing him that he would not be compromising with his
deeply-felt principles by taking the test. He at last consented to be ques-
tioned on his loyalty to Rowton and insisted that he be asked, "No you be-
lieve in Rowton?"
4. After a brief break for lunch the examination was given inone of the bed-
ro:ms 181 the apartment while Rowton waited in the living room. LIANG/3

appeared to be in reascably good spirits after the test, although
he was obviously emotionally strained by the experience. Rowton made
a date to see him again that evening at 21CO to talk things over in
a clamer atmosphere.
5. At that meeting with LIRING/3 Rowton explained that he had felt it
necessary to ascertain as objectively as possibly the extent of LIRING/3's
loyalty to him and he was happy to have scientific proof that LIRING/3
had not berayed him to the LIRING's. LIRING/3 stated that after it was

for Rowton, since he still felt very sensitive about having to accept money
from Rowton without being able to render commensurate services. He stress-

anything against Rowton's interest, as seior Albertini could prove with
the results of the SGSAILR. LIRING/3 promised in the future to follow Row-
ton's direction scrupulously and assured Rowton that he no longer felt
undes any compulsion to exaggerate or fabricate anything to impress Rowton.
6. Headquarters and the Station may find the SGSWIRL examination disapcom-
ting in its limited coverage, but it must be realized that LIRING/3's
initial reaction was entirely negative and at one point he thestened to
break off completely with Rowton because of the insult to his "dignity".
Although the SGSWIRL operator felt that from a professional standpoint it
would be better to administer the examination at another time when LIEING/3
was less emotionally upset, Rowton asked both him and LIRING/3 to go thru
with it on the spot, feeling that psychologically it was essential to
make LIRING/3 subit, even for a limited test. Rowt:n also feels that the
test did serve as a very favorably deterrent over LIRING/3 in the future,
when a second one can be more painlessly administered, in a calmer atmos-
phere. It, of course, also covered the very pertinent question of whether
LIRING/3 had been an LIRING doble agent or betrayed Rowton in any way.

BGWIRL Report on LIRING/3
1. Attached herewith is the EGSWIL. report (Idens u/s/c)
on LIRING/3.
2. Please note that the EGSWIL interviewer has made the
point that the principal misfortune in this interview probably
was that LIRING/3 was not tested on the fabrication of contacts
with the IDEN D's, which was thought to be the most probable
area of deception.

BOOTHON, we would be interested in hearing of any repurcussions
or change in attitude that may have resulted from LIRING/3's
having taken the test. We also are interested in the Station's
comments and recommendations as to the continued use of LIRING-3,
bearing in mind RONTON's recent report of LIRING SUSPICIOUS
L-3 may be working for BOFIRM.

Subject:
Report of LIKING/3 Suspect Affiliaticr with WC212M.
1. LIKING/3 reported to *owton at 0900 on 30 Cctc'er, 1967, that he
had finally menged to have a private talk with Rodolfo Reyes Cortes,
his Mexican chereographer friend, ou the afternoon of 27 October, 1967;
and that, ir the course of conversation, Rodolfo Reyes had revealed
to LIKING/3 in confidence think the reason why the LIKINGS had assumed
a rather cool attitude toward LIKING/3 over the past year. Rodolfo
Reyes explained that the last time he was in *avana he had heard rumors,
arong his friends in the Mexican colony, that LIKING/3 was worsing
"either for *CRIAM or the Cubans". Rodolfo went on to say that the
orgen of tans rumor, as far as he could ascortan, was the fact that
LIKING/3 had made two trips into Havana for no known speciicreason and
at his own expense. Rodolfo Reyes, indicating that he himself did not
believe the rumors or, at least, did not care whether they were true or
not, commented to LIKING/3 that other members of LIKING/3's profession
were naturally jealous of the success of anyone of their group and were
always quick to draw their own conclusions.
2. LIKING/3 commented to Rowton that, although this news had shaken hi
and LIKING/4 badly at the time, neither of them cared particularly whist
the LIKINGS thought of them, since their own conscience was clear. LI-
RING/3 added that it was important, however, to continue to develop his
commercial activity in Chiapas ( especially since Cdolfo Reyes' home is
by coincidence located in San Cristbal) so that word would gradually
filter back to the LIKINGS that he actually did have financial resources
outside his art production. LIKING/3 continued that obviously the LIKINGS
did not have any specific proof or they would long ago have cut off all
contact with him as well as LIKING/4. He concluded that since the LIKINGS
had certain suspicions, they naturally warned all his friends and forser
contacts (including, of course, Arnol Rodriguez) to avoid close contact
with him until their doubts could be resolved.
3. In reply to Rowton's query LIKING/3 stated that Rodolfo Reyes and Carmen
Nolina (separately) had commented to him that they were favorably impresseu
by Rowton and did not voice any suspicion of Rowton's bona fides (as a
Greek leftist businessman). Carmen Moaina, in fact, had gone so far as to
show some irritation that LIKING/3 had not introduced her to Rowton pre-
viously since she was anxious to develop some sort of lucrative business


2.
dealing with him. Carmen Molina commented to LIRING/3 that she felt
sure she could help Rowton in his business and political problems and
at the same time make a little much-needed money for her own living
expenses.
4. LIRING/3 continued that he had been maintaining discreet personal
contact with Carmen Lozada over the week-end ( he commented that LIRING/4
has already shown some signs of ealousy and therefore he ad to be careful
not to give her cause to distrust him). LIRING/3 stated that Carmen Lo-
zada had told him that her father, a well-to-do Mexican doctor residing
in Coyoca, had remarried tand that her step-mother was a Cuban scientist
with lead lived many year: in Mexico. She added that both her father and
step-mother were on excellent social terms with Ambassador Herrndez Aras.
She revealed that she had already notified her husband, Enrique Ramirez,
th.t she intended to divorce him, and she expected a storm of protest both
from him ( in Havana) and her father and step-mother, both of whoa were
"puritanic" despite their "progressive" convictions. She added that she
expected Enrique Ramirez to rush over from Havana as soon as he received
her letter and to appeal to her father and step-mother to save his mar-
risge. She, however, insisted to LIRING/3 that she had made up her mind
that she would go through with the divorce. She added that for this reason
she did not wish to live with her fsther and had decided to stay with.
her friend, Carmen Molina, until the divpce papers were through and the
storm had blown over. She added that she did not particularly like being
a house-guest in the smali arptment of Carmen Molina, but at the moment
she had no choice.
Wald Brant
Wallace B. Rowton

LATTER HASED HER FOUR PIECES OF APER WHICH HE INDICATED CON-
TAINED BONA FIDES ASD REGUEST FOR CUBAN HELP, WHICH HE WANTED

PPIRUMEN/LIRING-3
MARCH
ACTION REG/RES. REFERENCE
Action Required: FYI
Reference
Headquarters notes that on 9 August 1987 LIRING-3
was in contact via LIFEAT with one Electa LNU. Given
LIRING-3's artist background and the subject of
conversation - the visit of Rodolfo Heisler, a Swiss
artist, to Cuba - it is suggested that Electa LNU
might be Electa ARENAL (201-173795), the bother-in-law
of David ALFALO Squierces the well-known Mexican Communist
artist.
Andrew F. MERTON

FBRUNEN/Letter Received by LIRDC-3 from Rene * OUCHA Fumes
CTCIO REQUIRE. REPIFERS
FYI
Forwarded as Attachment One, berewith, is a report written a Calea
by Wallace B. ROWTDE dated 5 August 1967 about a letter recently
received by LIPING-3 from Rene OCHA Fumes, the Houduran revolutionary
to Favaa. Tornetil as at
photocopias of this letter. It does not look, from the sound of the
letter, that OCHOA's morale is too high.

Feyman A. Trayge

AUG 30 1981
5 August,
1. 1. 3 received/itzxz from bers Cehos Punc
145, Mexico 7, 17 after having been hase-cenried from Evamp to the
wife of a "ccapiero de troshige" of Cechos. Cepy being pouched.
2. In letter Cches states he understands L/3's sittucion "since it is
necessary to move ahead with the's own resources and to prove with
does". He addes that he hoped to send arxixixx
neves* but he still laboring under difficulties know- to L/3. He assures
L/3 that he has delivered L/3's last letter to 3xrxixixx the "Coppiaro"
(Amol horigique) but could not talk with him privately because of the
many visitors who had arrived that day. irmol's wife fuby told him that
they had received L/3's letters and had unered them ( L/316 told Row-
ten that he has never received these replies from Amol). Naby Rodriguez
also informed Cehoa that the "organismos corres collieets" eree going to
invite L/3 to Havana. Cchos promised L/3 that he would do whetzever be
could to expedite this trip ( hacer nuevas estiones).
2. Ccloa coccilains of the "realidades que ce han tocado vivir sauf" xxt
but indicates that he has no intention "rasign hisel" to Fresucrecy
conceating that it is necessary "procear La rupture, aprediendo a
aressare on Las procias wasa, taking the initiali and now expecting
sighting free enryone. He aide that he has finally cut the the
have bound'ith to Cuba and although he feals that be can do a great deal
there, but it is"infinitely small in cegarison with what he must do ex
curside". The assures L/3 that he is serious and that it concerns a
"planteniento srio".
3. Cchos also cautions L/3 against looing sight of the ultimate objective
in his comorcial activity, indicating that he has discussed this as-
pect of L/3's plars with "a friend" who knows sone of these questions
better that L/3. He aida that L/3's "assutos y actividades" interest
his intnesly, and the their situation is similar.

La Habana,27 de Julie de 1967.
Estimado Carliche:
Hey hace ns de un mes que recib tu earte, per les
conversaciones telefnicas sestenias habrs pociide comprender que
la dorora en contestarte se debe,ne precisamente a apetia de mi per-
to,sino felta de canales-ocuades para tal fin.
Esta to la l'envir por la gentilera de un compaere de
trabaje cuya espess va hata sa;diche sea de pase ye ne'le conerce a
